17:626:51222:7:15:80:539:102:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:26We  also  find  qualitatively  similar  results  when  using  actual  hours  worked  in  the  household  rather  than  usual
17:627:51348:15:11:72:540:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:hours per day as dependent variable when estimating the effect of risk.  Results are reported in the Appendix, Table
17:628:51464:11:0:72:88:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:C.4.
18:629:51470:0:17:72:493:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:discuss how we address some possible threats to identification at the end of this section.
18:630:51560:17:16:88:539:692:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In the absence of a labor market for girls and given intra-household substitution effects, maternal
18:631:51659:16:17:72:539:676:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wagewijtshould be a good proxy for the opportunity cost of time of girls and needs to be included
18:632:51756:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the structural hours equation.  Furthermore, we expect time allocation to depend on non-labor
18:633:51852:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income and all other household members’ labor incomeNijt(which excludes maternal labor income).
18:634:51947:17:16:71:539:626:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:These  two  variables  are  expected  to  capture  income  effects  on  time  in  school.   We  assume  that
18:635:52055:16:17:71:540:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:preferences for school can be captured by individual and household characteristicsXijt, i.e.  age,
18:636:52153:17:16:71:539:593:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:caste, religion, the number of children (in the household), household size, and land ownership, as
18:637:52251:16:16:71:539:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:measure of general household wealth.  Finally, the error term can be decomposed into a permanent
18:638:52347:16:17:71:539:561:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and two transitory components such that-ijt=μj+σjt+ηit, whereμjis a state-level fixed effect,
18:639:52440:17:16:71:498:544:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f3:σjtare village-level shocks andηitis a mean zero, strictly exogenous, idiosyncratic shock.
18:640:52530:16:17:88:539:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:As discussed above, the dependent variable will depend on maternal wages, if there is substitu-
18:641:52625:17:16:71:539:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tion between mother’s time and daughter’s time at home.  But adequately controlling for maternal
18:642:52721:16:17:71:539:495:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wages is challenging for a number of reasons.  First, observed wages are potentially endogenous to
18:643:52819:17:16:71:539:478:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:labor supply if wages reflect work effort as well as skills or ability, such that individuals who work
18:644:52921:16:16:71:539:462:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:longer hours are likely to get higher wages.  This is of concern particularly in the labor markets
18:645:53019:16:17:71:539:446:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of developed economies (see e.g. Keane, 2011).  In the context of low-skill agricultural wage work,
18:646:53118:17:16:71:539:429:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:however, we feel that this is less of an issue, because wage rates are determined by local conditions
18:647:53219:16:17:71:539:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rather than individual abilities (Rosenzweig, 1978; Rose, 2001; Jayachandran, 2006).  Second, both
18:648:53317:17:16:71:539:396:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wages and other household members’ labor income are endogenous to shocks.  There might be gen-
18:649:53411:16:17:71:539:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:eral equilibrium effects of shocks on wages (see e.g. Jayachandran, 2006):  if all households in the
18:650:53511:17:16:71:539:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:village supply more labor due to a shock, equilibrium wages should be lower than in the absence of
18:651:53609:16:16:71:539:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a shock.  We need to be aware of this when testing for effects of rainfall shocks on labor supply:  our
18:652:53712:16:17:71:539:331:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:predicted wages already account for general equilibrium effects of shocks on wages in the village
18:653:53809:17:16:71:539:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:economy,  and this might mask some of the effect of shocks on time allocation decisions.  Third,
18:654:53905:16:17:71:539:298:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wages are only observed for women who are currently in the labor market, such that we have to
18:655:53998:17:16:71:539:281:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:deal with missing wages for all women who are not participating in the labor market.  Potentially,
18:656:54096:16:17:71:539:265:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the  sample  of  workers  is  not  a  random  sub-sample  of  all  women,  such  that  we  have  to  account
18:657:54204:17:16:71:539:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for selection bias when imputing wages.  Fourth, most women in our sample reported working in
18:658:54297:16:17:71:539:232:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:different activities, at different wages.  Fifth, we have to deal with classical measurement error since
18:659:54401:17:16:71:456:215:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wages are mostly measured with considerable error in micro data (Keane, 2011).
18:660:54479:16:16:88:539:199:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We address the last three issues by predicting wages for all women in our sample.  Following
18:661:54571:16:17:71:539:183:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Blundell et al. (2007), we predict wages using a Heckman selection correction.  Since women report
18:662:54669:17:16:71:539:166:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:working in a number of different activities at different wage levels, we calculate weighted average
18:663:54768:16:0:71:539:150:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wages,  i.e.  calculate total income from all activities and divide it by the total number of hours
19:664:54869:0:30:72:318:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:worked.27Assume wages are determined as follows:
19:665:54917:30:30:99:539:679:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:lnwijt=δ0+δ1Xijt+δ2Rjt+μj+σjt+υit.(21)
19:666:54955:30:16:72:539:649:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In eq.  (21),Xijtcaptures age, age squared, caste, number of children in the household, religion,
19:667:55052:16:17:72:540:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:education,  land  ownership,  and  non-labor  income.Rjt,μjandσjtagain  capture  consumption
19:668:55144:17:16:71:539:616:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:risk, state fixed effects, and village-level rainfall shocks respectively.  The structural participation
19:669:55248:16:17:71:539:600:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:equation is similar to the wage equation, except that we add wages lnwijt, other household members’
19:670:55347:17:29:71:336:583:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:labor incomeNijt, and augmentXijtby marital status:
19:671:55398:29:30:99:539:554:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f3:pijt=α0+α1lnwijt+α2Xijt+α3Rjt+α4Nijt+μj+σjt+υit.(22)
19:672:55450:30:17:71:539:524:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Substitution eq.  (21) into the structural participation equation, gives the reduced-form participa-
19:673:55550:17:29:71:450:507:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tion equation, which is the selection equation for the Heckman selection model,
19:674:55629:29:30:99:539:478:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f3:pijt=a0+a1Xijt+a2Rjt+a3Nijt+μj+σjt+υit.(23)
19:675:55672:30:16:71:539:448:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We estimate this reduced-form participation equation first and then estimate the log hourly wage
19:676:55768:16:17:71:539:432:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:equation (21) including the inverse Mills ratio obtained from the estimated participation equation
19:677:55866:17:16:71:539:415:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(23).   In  this  approach,  the  wage  equation  is  identified  from  the  exclusion  of  other  household
19:678:55974:16:17:71:539:399:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:members’ labor income, and marital status from the wage equation, as well as from the normality
19:679:56069:17:16:71:539:382:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:assumption.28The structural hours equation (20) can then be estimated with imputed mothers’
19:680:56160:16:17:71:102:366:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wages.
19:681:56166:17:16:88:539:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Since our measure of consumption risk is not directly observed but predicted for each village,
19:682:56260:16:16:71:539:333:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:robust standard errors clustered at the village level probably overstate the estimator’s precision.
19:683:56359:16:17:71:539:317:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We therefore additionally conduct a percentile t-bootstrap method with cluster re-sampling at the
19:684:56456:17:16:71:539:300:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:village level, and 4,999 replications.  Predicted consumption risk is re-calculated for every bootstrap
19:685:56559:16:17:71:539:284:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:sample, and the distribution of t-statistics is obtained from regressing the outcome of interest in
19:686:56658:17:16:71:539:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:every bootstrap sample on a newly predicted risk variable. We report bootstrap p-values in addition
19:687:56757:16:17:71:328:251:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:to cluster-robust standard errors where appropriate.29
19:688:56811:17:16:88:539:234:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:As mentioned previously, the identifying assumption warrants some discussion.  Obviously, ir-
19:689:56904:16:17:71:539:218:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rigation systems are not placed randomly and one would expect wealthier villages to have more
19:690:56997:17:15:71:539:201:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:irrigation and lower consumption variability.  If wealthier villages have also higher school invest-
19:691:57097:15:15:80:539:186:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:27Alternatively one could use marginal wages, hence the lowest wages observed at which women supply a positive
19:692:57207:15:11:72:540:171:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:number of hours.  But we are worried that this measure cannot account for necessity-driven labor supply, i.e.  cases
19:693:57323:11:7:72:426:160:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:in which labor supply is high because wages are low in all activities that are performed.
19:694:57412:7:15:80:539:153:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:28Results are reported in the Appendix, Tables C.5 and C.6.  In our sample, 49 women report having a permanent
19:695:57522:15:11:72:540:138:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:job.  We assume that the wages of these women are determined by a different process than the casual wages observed
19:696:57636:11:11:72:540:127:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:for  the  rest  of  the  sample.   Therefore,  we  predict  wages  in  permanent  employment  separately  for  this  group.   As
19:697:57764:11:11:72:540:116:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the participation in permanent jobs cannot be predicted by other household members’ income, marital status or the
19:698:57877:11:11:72:540:105:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:number of children in the household, we predict these wages without adjusting for self-selection as reported in Table
19:699:57994:11:7:72:88:94:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:C.6.
19:700:57998:7:15:80:539:87:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:29The percentile-t cluster bootstrap has a better asymptotic refinement than the simple pairs cluster bootstrap,
19:701:58110:15:0:72:509:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:and seems more appropriate in a sample with 221 clusters.  For more details see Cameron and Miller (2015).
20:702:58218:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ments,  a  regression  of  school  time  on  predicted  consumption  risk  would  yield  biased  estimates.
20:703:58325:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:However, we control for different sources of household income and wealth in all our specifications
20:704:58423:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and allowing for more flexibility in the relationship between income and hours in school does not
20:705:58520:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:affect our results.  Additionally, for the subset of farm-households, we control for the share of area
20:706:58622:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that is irrigated on the farm, to avoid attributing the effect of reduced female irrigation work on
20:707:58721:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the farm to a reduction in consumption risk.  Again,  our results do not change.  The full set of
20:708:58818:16:38:72:286:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:robustness checks is discussed in Section 6.3.
20:709:58864:38:28:72:148:572:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:6    Results
20:710:58876:28:23:72:267:544:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:6.1Ex postresponses to shocks
20:711:58905:23:17:72:540:521:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In the following we want to test explicitly for the validity of two crucial assumptions made in the
20:712:59004:17:16:72:539:504:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:theoretical model.  First, anex  postlabor supply response by mothers to economic shocks.  And
20:713:59098:16:17:72:527:488:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:second, substitutability in maternal and daughter time in the performance of household chores.
20:714:59192:17:16:88:539:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We start by estimating the effect of rainfall shocks on maternal labor supply and time allocated
20:715:59288:16:17:72:540:455:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to households chores (Table 5).  As before, our sample consists of all mothers in our data to use
20:716:59385:17:16:72:540:438:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the available information most efficiently.  We control for age, caste, religion, education, household
20:717:59487:16:17:72:540:422:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:size, number of children in the household, land ownership, non-labor income, other member’s labor
20:718:59584:17:16:72:540:405:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income, and state fixed effects.  We do not control for risk, nor for wages, because we do not want
20:719:59683:16:16:72:540:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to mask the effect of shocks by conditioning on these variables.30We interact rainfall with a lean
20:720:59781:16:17:72:445:373:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:season dummy, to test explicitly for the timing of the labor supply response.31
20:721:59860:17:16:88:539:356:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Column  (1)  presents  the  effect  of  shocks  on  extensive  margin  labor  supply.   We  do  not  find
20:722:59965:16:17:72:540:340:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that  rainfall  affects  extensive  margin  labor  supply  in  either  season.   The  intensive  margin  labor
20:723:60075:17:16:72:540:323:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:supply response to shocks is shown in column (2).  While rainfall seems to have a positive (albeit
20:724:60173:16:17:72:540:307:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:not statistically significant) effect on labor supply in the agricultural peak seasons,  we find that
20:725:60274:17:16:72:539:290:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:negative rainfall shocks increase labor supply in the agricultural lean season, thusex  postto the
20:726:60372:16:16:72:540:274:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:full realization of rainfall outcomes.  As can be seen in column (3), the time allocation to household
20:727:60474:16:17:72:540:258:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:chores  seems  to  mirror  this,  although  the  coefficient  on  the  interaction  term  in  not  statistically
20:728:60586:17:16:72:123:241:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:significant.
20:729:60598:16:17:88:539:225:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:If maternal and daughter time are substitutes in the production of the home produced good,
20:730:60688:17:16:72:540:208:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:then any labor supply response of mothers to shocks should translate into the time their daughters
20:731:60786:16:17:72:540:192:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:allocate to household chores and spend in school.  We therefore test if shocks affect the time girls
20:732:60886:17:16:72:540:175:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spend  on  those  activities  in  different  seasons  in  Table  6.   Again,  we  also  control  for  age,  caste,
20:733:61000:16:16:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:religion, household size, number of children in the household, land ownership, non-labor income,
20:734:61096:16:17:72:325:143:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:other member’s labor income, and state fixed effects.
20:735:61149:17:16:88:539:126:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:As  shown  in  columns  (1)  and  (2),  rainfall  shocks,  seem  to  affect  time  in  school  only  at  the
20:736:61257:16:16:72:540:110:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:intensive margin – not at the extensive margin–, and only in the lean season, but not in the peak
20:737:61354:16:11:80:367:94:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:30Remember that we allow predicted wages to vary with rainfall levels.
20:738:61424:11:0:80:493:83:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:31For a more direct interpretation of the interaction term, log rainfall is normalized to a mean of zero.
21:739:61531:0:17:72:539:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:seasons.  The seasonality of the effect is consistent with the theoretical model:ex  postto shocks,
21:740:61630:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:mothers have to work in order to generate additional income,  and this puts greater pressure on
21:741:61725:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f4:the daughter to reduce time in school and to perform household duties.  The fact that anex  post
21:742:61821:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:response to shocks only materializes at the intensive margin is consistent with the notion of fixed
21:743:61920:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:costs  of  school  attendance:   since  those  costs  had  to  be  incurred  already  at  the  time  of  shock
21:744:62030:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:realization, an intensive margin response is “less costly” than an extensive margin response.  Again,
21:745:62131:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the time allocation to household chores mirrors the effect on school time, as reported in column
21:746:62227:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(3).  On average, girls spend more time on household chores in the lean season than in the peak
21:747:62322:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:season, and only at very high rainfall outcomes that difference approaches zero and is no longer
21:748:62418:16:33:72:189:561:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:statistically significant.32
21:749:62446:33:23:72:421:528:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:6.2    The effect of consumption risk on girls’ time in school
21:750:62508:23:16:72:540:505:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We continue by examining how risk affects the time girls spend in school.  We have seasonal data
21:751:62604:16:17:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for 4,306 girls in the age group 6 to 16.  Our model predicts a negative effect of consumption risk
21:752:62703:17:16:72:540:472:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:on time in school if there is a high degree of dynamic complementarity in the education production
21:753:62801:16:17:72:540:456:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:function.  At substitution elasticities of one, as observed in the YLS data from India, our model
21:754:62898:17:16:72:540:439:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:predicts a negative effect of risk only if household utility is increasing linearly in the stock of human
21:755:63003:16:17:72:115:423:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:capital.33
21:756:63013:17:16:88:539:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Table 7 reports OLS estimates of the effect of risk on time in school at the extensive margin in
21:757:63109:16:17:72:540:390:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:columns (1) and (2), and at the intensive margin in columns (3) and (4).  We use two variables to
21:758:63206:17:16:72:540:373:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:proxy consumption risk, i.e.  the interquartile range as well as the standard deviation of predicted
21:759:63306:16:16:72:540:357:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:log consumption.  As discussed above, we control for predicted wages of mothers and for individual
21:760:63404:16:17:72:540:341:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and  household-level  socio-economic  characteristics  in  all  our  specifications.   In  order  to  account
21:761:63513:17:16:72:540:324:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for the effect of non-labor income on time allocation, we include a measure of all other household
21:762:63611:16:17:72:539:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:members’ labor income as well as total household non-labor income per capita.34We also control
21:763:63705:17:16:71:539:291:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for rainfall shocks, state fixed effects, and a lean-season fixed effect.  Standard errors are clustered
21:764:63809:16:17:71:539:275:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:at the village level; i.e.  the level of variation of the main explanatory variable.  Bootstrap p-values
21:765:63913:17:16:71:262:258:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:are reported at the bottom of the table.
21:766:63953:16:16:88:539:242:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We find that risk considerably reduces time in school at the extensive margin, but not at the
21:767:64046:16:17:71:539:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:intensive margin.  This suggests that girls drop out of school temporarily or permanently in the
21:768:64142:17:16:71:539:209:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:presence of risk, while there is little scope for adjusting the time in school at the intensive margin.
21:769:64245:16:17:71:539:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This result suggests the presence of an (unmodeled) fixed cost of school attendance, that causes
21:770:64341:17:16:71:539:176:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:households to withdraw a child from school entirely when faced with higher risk.  According to our
21:771:64439:16:16:71:539:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:estimates, a one standard deviation increase in the interquartile range of predicted log consumption
21:772:64539:16:15:80:539:144:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:32Note that the coefficient of the interaction term is not statistically significant, still marginal effects of the lean
21:773:64659:15:7:72:540:129:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:season are negative and significant at low rainfall levels, and close to zero (and not significant) and high rainfall levels.
21:774:64784:7:15:80:539:122:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:33Remember, a positive effect of risk on time in school could either stem from high risk aversion with respect to
21:775:64897:15:11:72:540:107:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the final stock of human capital or from perfect substitutability of school times in the production of human capital
21:776:65013:11:7:72:291:96:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:at moderate levels of risk aversion with respect toH2.
21:777:65067:7:0:80:420:89:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:34Other household members’ labor income excludes the labor income of the mother.
22:778:65149:0:17:72:539:709:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:(0.033) reduces the probability that girls attend school by 5.8 percentage points in every season.35
22:779:65249:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This effect is statistically significant at the 1% level for both risk variables (c.f.  bootstrap p-values
22:780:65355:16:17:72:198:676:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:at the bottom of Table 7).
22:781:65381:17:16:88:539:659:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Mothers’ wages seem to be positively associated with time in school at the extensive margin,
22:782:65473:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and negatively at the intensive margin, although the coefficient is statistically significant only at the
22:783:65578:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:extensive margin. This suggests that the income effect, rather than the intra-household substitution
22:784:65678:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effect dominates at the extensive margin.  However, due to the fact that we have to predict wages,
22:785:65776:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:we  caution  against  a  causal  interpretation  of  the  coefficient  on  mothers’  wages.   The  remaining
22:786:65884:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:coefficients have the expected sign:  as girls get older, they are less likely to attend school.  Girls
22:787:65987:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:belonging  to  scheduled  castes  and  tribes  are  less  likely  to  attend  school,  while  Hindu  girls  are
22:788:66098:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:more likely to attend school than girls from other religions.  As non-labor income increases,  the
22:789:66196:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:probability  of  attending  school,  as  well  as  the  time  spent  in  school  increases,  again  pointing  to
22:790:66308:17:16:72:141:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income effects.
22:791:66323:16:17:88:539:495:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A potential concern about these measured effects of risk is that risk affects the future returns
22:792:66419:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to  human  capital  as  well  as  the  opportunity  cost  of  time,  which  is  the  focus  of  our  model.   As
22:793:66531:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:noted above, this concern is one of the reasons why we focus on daughters, who are likely to leave
22:794:66629:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the village following marriage.  Nonetheless, because risk is likely correlated across space, marriage
22:795:66731:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:market risk may well be correlated with consumption risk in the village of origin.  We address this
22:796:66830:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:problem by adapting a strategy from Foster and Rosenzweig (1999).  In particular, that paper uses
22:797:66927:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a radius of 67km to define the marriage market (the 90th percentile of the marriage distance).  It
22:798:67025:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:then distinguishes the returns to human capital for boys (that in the village) and the returns to
22:799:67122:17:16:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:human capital for girls (among sample villages in the broader marriage market).  In this case, we
22:800:67219:16:16:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:control  for  the  average  risk  among  sample  villages  within  67km  of  each  village  of  interest.   We
22:801:67329:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:exclude the village of interest from this mean and drop those villages in which there are no other
22:802:67427:17:16:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:sample villages in the marriage market.  Table 8 reports the resulting estimates.  The coefficient
22:803:67525:16:17:72:540:298:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:on marriage-market risk is close to zero and its inclusion does not substantially affect the point
22:804:67623:17:16:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:estimate on the coefficient of interest.  Thus, as posited in our model the risk estimates appear to
22:805:67723:16:32:72:540:265:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:reflect the consequences of risk for the opportunity cost of time of daughters while they are children.
22:806:67826:32:24:72:211:233:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:6.3    Robustness checks
22:807:67850:24:16:72:540:209:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:As girls spend less time in school in the presence of risk, overall household utility can be increased
22:808:67952:16:17:72:540:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:if the daughter spends her available time on household activities.  We test this prediction in Table
22:809:68052:17:16:72:540:176:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:9.  As before columns (1) and (2) report the extensive margin effects, and columns (3) and (4) the
22:810:68150:16:17:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:intensive margin effects.  Consistent with the theoretical model, we find evidence that risk increases
22:811:68252:17:16:72:540:143:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the time girls spend on household activities.  Again the effect is only statistically significant at the
22:812:68356:16:16:72:540:127:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:extensive margin.  The magnitude of the coefficient suggests that a one standard deviation increase
22:813:68455:16:17:72:540:111:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the interquartile range of predicted log consumption (0.033) increases the probability to perform
22:814:68555:17:15:80:539:94:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:35Likewise, an increase in the standard deviation of predicted log consumption by one standard deviation (0.025)
22:815:68667:15:0:72:363:79:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:reduces the probability that girls are in school by 5.2 percentage points.
23:816:68743:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:household chores by 2.9 percentage points.  A one standard deviation increase in our alternative risk
23:817:68844:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:variable, the standard deviation of predicted log consumption, increases the probability to perform
23:818:68943:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:household chores by 3.4 percentage points.  The effects are statistically significant at the 10% and
23:819:69043:17:16:72:384:659:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:at the 5% level, respectively, according to the bootstrap p-values.
23:820:69110:16:17:88:539:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The hypothesis that risk reduces time in school rests on the assumption that girls have to fill
23:821:69205:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in for their mothers in household duties when faced with shocks.  As the probability to perform
23:822:69300:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:household work strongly increases with age, this also suggests that the effect of risk should be more
23:823:69401:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:pronounced for older girls.36And this is precisely what we find, when we split the sample by age
23:824:69497:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:group.  The coefficient on both risk variables almost doubles in magnitude when moving from the
23:825:69592:16:17:72:371:561:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:group of girls below the age of 11 to girls aged 11 and above.37
23:826:69656:17:16:88:539:544:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:One concern could be that the observed effect of risk is not really a forward looking risk effect.
23:827:69754:16:17:71:539:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Suppose past school time increases the marginal return to current school time, and past school time
23:828:69853:17:16:71:539:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:is lower in riskier areas due to more regularly occurring shocks.  Then current school time should
23:829:69951:16:17:71:539:495:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:also be lower given that there was more variation in school time previously.  In order to address this
23:830:70053:17:16:71:539:478:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:concern, we condition current school time on the stock of human capital – measured as the highest
23:831:70150:16:16:71:539:462:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:level of schooling achieved so far.  Given concerns about endogeneity, we instrument the stock of
23:832:70247:16:17:71:539:446:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:human capital by rainfall shocks occurring in the school history of a child.  Our results are robust
23:833:70347:17:16:71:238:429:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:to the inclusion of these controls.38
23:834:70384:16:17:88:539:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We also address the concern that our risk variables might capture wealth rather than variability
23:835:70480:17:16:71:539:396:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in consumption.  First, we test if dropping wealth and income controls, controlling more flexibly for
23:836:70581:16:17:71:539:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:these variables, or allowing for the effect of risk to vary with land ownership (as proxy for wealth)
23:837:70682:17:16:71:540:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:affects our results.39None of these specifications alters our main results.  Second, we test if there
23:838:70783:16:16:71:539:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:is a direct relationship between area under irrigation and the probability of attending school for
23:839:70881:16:17:71:539:331:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the subset of farm-households, and if this is driving our results.  Again, controlling for the share
23:840:70981:17:16:71:539:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of area that is irrigated on the farm, its square or the interaction with consumption risk does not
23:841:71080:16:17:71:162:298:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:affect our results.40
23:842:71101:17:16:88:539:281:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Finally, if boys also have to fill in for mothers in household chores, and preferences for boys’
23:843:71197:16:17:72:540:265:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:human capital are similar to preferences for girls’ human capital, then we would expect to see a
23:844:71293:17:16:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:similar effect of risk on boys.  On the other hand, as noted above, boys are more likely than girls to
23:845:71395:16:17:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:remain in the village as adults and risk may affect the returns to human capital in the future.  Such
23:846:71496:17:16:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effects might be either positive or negative, depending, among other things, on whether education
23:847:71593:16:16:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:is seen as way to diversify income risk.  We therefore test if shocks affect the time boys spend in
23:848:71692:16:17:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:school, on household chores and on the labor market and whether risk also affects the schooling
23:849:71787:17:16:72:540:166:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of boys.  We find similar effects of rainfall shocks on boys to those on girls:  conditional on being
23:850:71888:16:15:80:539:150:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:36Figure B.1 in the Appendix plots the probability of performing household chores and of being in school by age.
23:851:72000:15:10:72:540:135:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:The probability that girls perform household duties increases continuously with age, while the probability of being
23:852:72115:10:8:72:244:125:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:in school starts to decline at the age of 11.
23:853:72160:8:11:80:286:117:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:37Results are reported in the Appendix, Table C.7.
23:854:72210:11:11:80:286:106:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:38Results are reported in the Appendix, Table C.8.
23:855:72260:11:11:80:286:95:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:39Results are reported in the Appendix, Table C.9.
23:856:72310:11:0:80:291:84:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:40Results are reported in the Appendix, Table C.10.
24:857:72363:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in school, a negative rainfall shock reduces the time boys spend in school in the agricultural lean
24:858:72462:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:season, and increases the time they spend on household activities.  Interestingly, boys do not seem
24:859:72561:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to spend more time, but rather less time on the labor market in the lean season when the household
24:860:72659:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:is faced with a negative rainfall shock, perhaps reflecting a wage effect.  However, when we test for
24:861:72760:16:17:72:539:643:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:the effect of risk on boys,  we fail to find a statistically significant effect on school attendance.41
24:862:72863:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This result could reflect differences in the concavity of household preferences in the stock of human
24:863:72964:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:capital of their sons versus their daughters or, as posited above, differences in the return to human
24:864:73065:17:16:72:143:593:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:capital by risk.
24:865:73081:16:16:88:539:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To summarize, our results suggest a strong and robust relationship between risk at the household
24:866:73177:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:level and girls’ time allocation, both to school and to household chores, which seem to be driven by
24:867:73277:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f3:ex  postlabor supply responses of mothers to income shocks and the intra-household substitution
24:868:73372:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in  household  work.   These  effects  are  very  harmful  to  the  accumulation  of  human  capital,  and
24:869:73478:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:potentially for future earnings of these girls.  We will discuss the potential role for public policy
24:870:73579:16:32:72:323:495:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:later and now look at some alternative explanations.
24:871:73631:32:24:72:247:463:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:6.4    Alternative explanations
24:872:73662:24:16:72:540:439:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:An alternative explanation to the effect of consumption risk on daughters’ time in school might be
24:873:73760:16:17:72:540:423:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that her mother is simply trying to work more in order to increase savings, and therefore spends
24:874:73856:17:16:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:less time on household chores.  That households tend to save more in the presence of uninsured risk
24:875:73955:16:17:72:540:390:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:is by now well established.  However, it is unclear to which extent this affects labor supply decisions.
24:876:74059:17:16:72:540:373:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Typically,  the literature has looked at foregone current consumption for the sake of higher (and
24:877:74156:16:16:72:540:357:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:more secure) future consumption (Zeldes, 1989; Deaton, 1991).  On the other side, one might think
24:878:74253:16:17:72:540:341:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that women would tend to work harder in order to accumulate savings more easily.  If this is the
24:879:74349:17:16:72:540:324:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:case, then we must worry that the observed effect on child outcomes is only an artifact of maternal
24:880:74448:16:17:72:180:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:labor supply decisions.
24:881:74471:17:16:88:539:291:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Table  10  shows  the  effect  of  risk  on  maternal  time  allocation.   In  columns  (1)  and  (2),  we
24:882:74577:16:17:72:540:275:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:test if risk affects maternal labor supply at the extensive margin, and do not find any statistically
24:883:74678:17:16:72:540:258:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:significant effect.  In columns (3) and (4), and (5) and (6) we test if risk affects hours worked on the
24:884:74782:16:16:72:540:242:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:labor market and on household chores, conditional on being in the labor force.  We do find some
24:885:74877:16:17:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:– albeit weak – evidence that mothers, conditional on being in the labor force, spend more time
24:886:74972:17:16:72:540:209:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:on the labor market and less time on household chores in the presence of risk.  However, only the
24:887:75069:16:17:72:540:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effect of risk on time allocated to household chores is statistically significant at the 10% level, when
24:888:75173:17:16:72:540:176:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:inference  is  based  on  the  bootstrap  p-values.   The  bootstrap  p-values  on  intensive  margin  labor
24:889:75281:16:17:72:255:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:supply are 15% and 22%, respectively.
24:890:75318:17:16:88:539:143:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:An alternative explanation for an effect of risk on maternal time allocation is that risk reduces
24:891:75415:16:16:72:540:127:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the time girls spend in school and increases their time in household activities, combined with the
24:892:75513:16:16:72:540:111:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:intra-household substitution in home production.  As a household can increase utility by increasing
24:893:75612:16:15:80:539:95:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:41Because the main substitution seems to work through household chores, we again control for maternal wages in
24:894:75722:15:0:72:429:80:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the school time regression.  Results are reported in the Appendix, Tables C.11 and C.12.
25:895:75812:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:consumption of the home produced as well as the market produced good, mothers might decrease
25:896:75904:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the time they spend on household activities and work more on the labor market, when their daughter
25:897:76002:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:spend more time on household chores.  We can thus not conclusively identify the underlying causal
25:898:76099:17:16:72:375:659:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:mechanisms by looking at the time allocation of mothers alone.
25:899:76161:16:17:88:539:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Another, admittedly imperfect, way to approach this issue is to test if households tend to save
25:900:76256:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:more in the presence of uninsured risk.  Since households in this context typically have no access
25:901:76354:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to  good  liquid  savings,  our  very  crude  measure  of  savings  is  the  difference  between  household
25:902:76461:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income and household consumption, which is probably measured with considerable error and also
25:903:76554:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:becomes negative as households dissave when faced with a shock.  We therefore restrict the sample
25:904:76651:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to households with positive savings.  As reported in Table 11, however, we do not find any evidence
25:905:76750:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that households tend to save more as risk increases.  If anything savings seem to decrease with risk.
25:906:76851:16:17:88:539:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:More importantly, in a multi-period model with known risk distribution, the effect of risk on
25:907:76944:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:incremental savings should be small in any given period because savings accumulation is substi-
25:908:77039:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tutable across time.  In contrast, any child human capital response is complementary over time and
25:909:77137:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tied to child age.  We thus have both theoretical and empirical arguments against the explanation
25:910:77234:16:16:72:487:462:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that observed effects on girls’ school time are driven by precautionary savings motives.
25:911:77322:16:17:88:539:446:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Above we used marriage market data to explore the possibility that the returns to education
25:912:77413:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:vary with risk.  An alternative approach is to test directly whether the wage return to education
25:913:77510:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:varies with risk. We do not find any evidence that risk in fact reduces the returns to education either
25:914:77613:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for men or for women.  Of course, this approach does not account for other possible consequences of
25:915:77712:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:risk such as the returns to entrepreneurship or the returns to migration.  But it is at least consistent
25:916:77816:17:16:72:461:363:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:with the idea that our effect of interest is not driven by the return to schooling.42
25:917:77901:16:16:88:539:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Finally, one might worry that any schooling response of girls is driven by supply side constraints
25:918:77999:16:17:71:539:331:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rather than demand side factors. For example, it could be that our risk measure is picking up general
25:919:78100:17:16:71:539:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:differences in village wealth which correlates with irrigation as well as with the supply of education.
25:920:78203:16:17:71:539:298:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We therefore test if our results are affected by controlling for the number of primary or secondary
25:921:78302:17:16:71:539:281:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:schools,  by  the  degree  of  teacher  absenteeism  or  the  availability  of  the  mid-day  meal  scheme  in
25:922:78412:16:38:71:318:265:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:schools.  None of these variables affect our results.43
25:923:78467:38:22:71:539:227:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:7    Simulating the effect of the NREGS on consumption risk, labor
25:924:78533:22:27:96:378:205:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:supply and human capital accumulation
25:925:78570:27:17:71:539:178:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Given the magnitude of the effects of risk observed above, it seems worthwhile to explore potential
25:926:78669:17:16:71:539:161:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:policy tools to mediate these.  Obviously, any policy tool that helps farmers insure against agricul-
25:927:78770:16:17:71:539:145:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tural production risk, could be a viable option.  But as Mobarak and Rosenzweig (2013) pointed
25:928:78864:17:16:71:539:128:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:out,  providing insurance to farmers might actually increase overall (consumption) risk in village
25:929:78962:16:16:71:539:112:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:economies as farmers become more risk taking in their production decisions.  This would then be
25:930:79057:16:11:80:286:96:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:42C.f.  with Tables C.13 and C.14 in the Appendix.
25:931:79107:11:0:80:265:85:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:43As reported in Table C.15 in the Appendix.
26:932:79153:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:particularly  harmful  for  the  poorest  households  with  no  own  land  and  no  access  to  agricultural
26:933:79261:17:16:72:120:692:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:insurance.
26:934:79271:16:17:88:539:676:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:An alternative could be an income-smoothing policy, such as the Indian National Rural Em-
26:935:79360:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ployment  Guarantee  Scheme,  that  was  introduced  in  rural  India  in  2006.   The  National  Rural
26:936:79463:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Employment Guarantee Act is India’s flagship anti-poverty program; it entitles every household in
26:937:79560:17:16:72:494:626:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rural India to a maximum of 100 days of employment per year at state minimum wages.
26:938:79643:16:17:88:539:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This  scheme  can  affect  schooling  decisions  through  two  effects:   first,  the  NREGS  provides
26:939:79745:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:employment at higher wages than casual agricultural wages, which affected both total labor supply
26:940:79842:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and the amount of labor supplied to the private sector,  and therewith equilibrium wages in the
26:941:79937:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:private sector (Berg et al., 2012; Imbert and Papp, 2015).  As documented by Shah and Steinberg
26:942:80032:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(2015) the resulting increase in wages did pull more women into the labor force and reduced the
26:943:80127:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:time women spent on household chores.  Due to intra-household substitution in home production,
26:944:80221:17:16:72:539:511:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:this also raised the opportunity costs of time for girls and reduced the time they spent in school.44
26:945:80322:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Second,  the  NREGS  reduces  consumption  risk  in  rural  areas,  because  it  provides  a  minimum
26:946:80423:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:amount of employment at a fixed wage level independently of rainfall shocks.  Assuming income
26:947:80516:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effects dominate maternal wage allocation, the fact that the wage does not fall during periods of
26:948:80613:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:need is likely to reduce the magnitude of the labor supply response of women relative to case in
26:949:80709:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:which there are general equilibrium wage effects.  This effect should in turn reduce the extent of
26:950:80807:16:17:72:539:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the response among girlsex post.  This lower response, in turn, increases the return to first-period
26:951:80907:17:16:72:129:396:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:school time.
26:952:80919:16:17:88:539:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The following simulation of the effects of the NREGS seeks to shed light on the importance of
26:953:81012:17:16:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:this second mechanism and is intended to complement existing empirical evidence on the short-
26:954:81105:16:16:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:term impact of the NREGS on schooling outcomes.  We expect that the risk mitigating effect of
26:955:81198:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the NREGS is internalized by households only after a certain period of time.  Therefore this effect
26:956:81297:17:16:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cannot  be  captured  by  impact  evaluations  that  explore  the  sequenced  phase-in  of  the  NREGS
26:957:81399:16:17:72:539:298:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and which can thus only provide information about the short-time effects of the program.45This
26:958:81493:17:16:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:simulation is intended to provide insights about potential long-run effects associated with public
26:959:81591:16:17:72:249:265:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:works programs such as the NREGS.
26:960:81624:17:16:88:539:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To estimate the importance of the risk-reduction effect of the NREGS on time in school, we use
26:961:81718:16:17:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the Socio-Economic Profiles of Rural Households in India (SEPRI) data of 2014.  It is a follow-up
26:962:81815:17:16:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:survey to the REDS that was collected in 8 states of India:  Andhra Pradesh, Bihar, Chhattisgarh,
26:963:81912:16:16:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Haryana, Jharkhand, Madhya Pradesh, Tamil Nadu and Rajasthan.  It samples the entire popula-
26:964:82004:16:17:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tion of the REDS survey villages, but applies a questionnaire that is considerably shorter than in
26:965:82102:17:16:72:131:166:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:the REDS.46
26:966:82113:16:16:88:539:150:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Using the SEPRI data, we estimate the extent to which the presence of the NREGS, or more
26:967:82201:16:11:80:428:134:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:44Li and Sekhri (2013) also find evidence that the NREGS reduced school attendance.
26:968:82284:11:15:80:539:123:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:45Given that we estimate the wage elasticity of different activities, we could also simulate a potential wage effect
26:969:82400:15:11:72:540:108:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:of the NREGS, and attempt to predict a net effect.  But due to the cross-sectional nature of our data we do not trust
26:970:82517:11:11:72:540:97:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the wage coefficients to be precise enough to perform such an analysis and restrict ourselves to an analysis of the risk
26:971:82637:11:7:72:202:86:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:mitigating effect of the NREGS.
26:972:82668:7:0:80:416:79:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:46Summary statistics of the SEPRI data are shown in Table C.16 in the Appendix.
27:973:82749:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:specifically, the amount of employment generated within the NREGS in a given year, mediates the
27:974:82844:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effect of rainfall on household consumption.  Formally, we estimate the same equation as in Table
27:975:82941:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:3,  but  now  add  employment  per  capita  (in  person-days)  generated  in  a  given  village  within  the
27:976:83049:17:16:72:539:659:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:NREGS and its interaction with rainfall to the estimation.  Results are reported in Table 12.47We
27:977:83146:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:find that a one unit increase in employment per capita generated, reduces the effect of rainfall on
27:978:83245:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:consumption by 4.7 percentage points.48We use these results to predict the standard deviation of
27:979:83341:16:17:72:462:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:predicted log consumption at different levels of employment per capita generated.
27:980:83422:17:16:88:553:593:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To make our simulation comparable to existing studies, we need an estimate of average employment-
27:981:83519:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:days created within the NREGS for the time period of these studies.  The most well documented
27:982:83612:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:paper on the effect of the NREGS is by Imbert and Papp (2015).  Using data from 2004/05 and
27:983:83703:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:2007/08,  the  authors  estimate  the  effects  of  the  NREGS  on  casual  wages.   In  the  financial  year
27:984:83812:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:2007/08,  the  NREGS  was  implemented  in  330  (out  of  625)  rural  districts  of  India,  covering  a
27:985:83918:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:population  of  642  Million.49In  that  year,  the  total  amount  of  employment-days  created  within
27:986:84022:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the NREGS was 1,435.9 Million (Ministry of Rural Development, 2012).  The average number of
27:987:84113:17:16:72:516:478:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:person-days of employment generated per capita was thus 2.24 in the implementing districts.
27:988:84204:16:16:88:539:462:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In the SEPRI data, average employment creation per capita within the NREGS is 0.76, with
27:989:84292:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a standard deviation of 1.23, in 2011/12.  At the mean of irrigation and the minimum of NREGS
27:990:84385:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:employment  creation  (i.e.   zero  employment),  an  increase  in  NREGS  employment  by  2.24  days
27:991:84486:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:per  capita  would  reduce  the  standard  deviation  of  log  consumption  by  0.029  on  average.   This
27:992:84592:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:corresponds to a 43.0% reduction in risk as compared to the baseline of no NREGS employment in
27:993:84686:16:17:72:180:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:2014 (c.f.  Table C.16).
27:994:84710:17:16:88:539:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:With these estimates we can simulate the risk-mitigating effect of the NREGS on the probability
27:995:84805:16:16:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that girls attend school.  Using the estimates presented in Table 7,  column (2), the reduction in
27:996:84903:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:risk exposure by 43% of the mean – as can be attributed to the NREGS – increases the probability
27:997:84999:17:16:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of attending school by 2.9 percentage points.  Our simulation thus suggests that an employment
27:998:85093:16:17:72:540:298:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:guarantee such as the NREGS can have positive effects on girls’ human capital accumulation by
27:999:85186:17:16:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:reducing consumption risk.  However, from previous literature we know that the extent to which
27:1000:85280:16:17:72:540:265:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:such programs affect adult’s wages is also critical.  If the wage effect outweighs the risk reducing
27:1001:85380:17:16:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effect, or in other words, if the risk reducing effect is not high enough to offset the negative effect of
27:1002:85486:16:17:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:increasing wages, then an employment guarantee such as the NREGS decreases school attendance
27:1003:85578:17:15:72:416:215:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:not only in the first years of program implementation, but permanently.
27:1004:85649:15:15:80:539:200:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:47The rainfall data covers the agricultural year 2012/13, which is presumably the period that determines consump-
27:1005:85762:15:11:72:540:185:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:tion outcomes in 2014.  Due to data limitations we have to use the amount of employment generated in the financial
27:1006:85876:11:7:72:362:174:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:year 2011/12.  The NREGS data of 2012/13 is incomplete in the survey.
27:1007:85945:7:15:80:539:167:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:48In both regressions, we drop 1,786 observations in order to reduce the influence of outliers.  Outliers are detected
27:1008:86063:15:11:72:540:152:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:using the DFBETA statistic for the share of irrigated land and the usual cutoff value of 2/sqrt(N), with N being the
27:1009:86179:11:7:72:168:141:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:number of observations.
27:1010:86202:7:15:80:539:134:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:49This  is  the  projected  population  as  of  March  2007  of  Phase  I  and  Phase  II  districts,  thus  all  districts  that
27:1011:86331:15:11:72:540:119:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:implemented the NREGS by May 2008. To get the population estimates, we apply the India-wide projected population
27:1012:86443:11:11:72:540:108:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:growth rate to the Census 2001 population count of these districts.  The projected growth rate was obtained from
27:1013:86555:11:0:72:249:97:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:National Commission on Population (2006).
28:1014:86598:0:28:72:180:709:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:8    Conclusions
28:1015:86614:28:16:72:540:681:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This paper develops a model of human capital investment that highlights the joint effect of consump-
28:1016:86714:16:17:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tion risk and dynamic complementarity in the production of human capital.  The model highlights
28:1017:86809:17:16:72:540:648:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that risk affects the time girls spend in school as long as three conditions are met.  First, there is
28:1018:86911:16:16:72:540:632:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:dynamic complementarity in the education production function.  Second, there is substitutability
28:1019:87007:16:17:72:540:616:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of maternal and daughter time in home production, and third, mother’s respond to income shocks
28:1020:87101:17:16:72:263:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:by increasing their labor supplyex post.
28:1021:87141:16:17:88:539:583:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Under these three conditions the effect of risk is consistently negative as long as household utility
28:1022:87242:17:16:72:540:566:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:is assumed to increase linearly in the daughter’s final stock of human capital.  If the household’s
28:1023:87341:16:17:72:540:550:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:marginal utility decreases with increasing stocks of human capital – in other words, if the household
28:1024:87442:17:16:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:is risk-averse with respect to the stock of human capital – the effect of risk on school investment is
28:1025:87544:16:16:72:540:517:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:negative at very high levels of dynamic complementarity, and turns positive as school investments
28:1026:87641:16:17:72:322:501:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of different time periods become more substitutable.
28:1027:87693:17:16:88:539:484:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Using the Young Lives Data of India, we estimate the elasticity of substitution in school times
28:1028:87788:16:17:72:540:468:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:between periods.  Using a non-linear instrumental variables approach, we cannot reject substitution
28:1029:87887:17:16:72:540:451:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:elasticities of one.  At this level, the model predicts a negative effect of risk only if household utility
28:1030:87994:16:17:72:540:435:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:increases linearly in human capital.  In contrast, if household utility is log-linear in human capital,
28:1031:88097:17:16:72:307:418:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the predicted effect of risk on school time is zero.
28:1032:88149:16:17:88:539:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We test the model’s assumptions and implications in the context of rural India, and find strong
28:1033:88244:17:16:72:540:385:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:evidence for a negative effect of risk on the probability that girls attend school.  While the main
28:1034:88343:16:16:72:540:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:focus of this paper lies on school attendance, we also find evidence that girls who are more exposed
28:1035:88443:16:17:72:540:353:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to risk also spend more time on household activities.  Taken together, these findings point to the
28:1036:88541:17:16:72:383:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:detrimental consequences of risk on human capital accumulation.
28:1037:88604:16:17:88:539:320:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This  effect  can  only  be  explained  by  dynamic  complementarity  in  the  production  of  human
28:1038:88704:17:16:72:540:303:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:capital, and by a household utility that increases linearly (or close to linearly) in the human capital
28:1039:88807:16:17:72:540:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:stock of the child.  Such a utility function is consistent with overlapping-generations models as long
28:1040:88909:17:16:72:540:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:as we account for households expectations of a convex relationship between years of schooling and
28:1041:89006:16:16:72:141:254:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:future income.
28:1042:89020:16:17:88:539:238:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:These findings contribute to a better understanding of the consequences of dynamic comple-
28:1043:89110:17:16:72:540:221:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:mentarity in the production of human capital.  Dynamic complementarity not only calls for early
28:1044:89205:16:17:72:540:205:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:lifetime interventions in order to remedy the consequences of shocks, and to reduce inequality of op-
28:1045:89306:17:16:72:540:188:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:portunities.  We also need to think of better ways to support households, particularly in developing
28:1046:89406:16:17:72:369:172:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:countries, in dealing with various sources of consumption risk.
28:1047:89469:17:16:88:539:155:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Arguably,  a public works program could be a policy that supports households in contexts of
28:1048:89560:16:16:72:540:139:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:high exposure to climate risk, because it off-sets the negative effects of rainfall shocks on wages and
28:1049:89663:16:17:72:540:123:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:incomes.  We simulate the effect of the National Rural Employment Guarantee Scheme on the time
28:1050:89757:17:16:72:540:106:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:allocation of girls.  We estimate the extent to which NREGS reduces variability in consumption
28:1051:89851:16:17:72:540:90:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and use this reduction to simulate the effect of the program on girls’ time in school.  We find that
28:1052:89951:17:0:72:540:73:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the program would increase girls’ school attendance by 2.9 percentage points, holding the level of
29:1053:90051:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wages fixed.  These results suggest that income transfers,  either in the form of cash transfers or
29:1054:90150:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:public works programs could increase investments in human capital by reducing consumption risk.
29:1055:90245:16:17:88:539:676:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:However such programs need to be carefully designed.  As shown in the case of the NREGS, the
29:1056:90337:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:fact that public works wages were above market wages let to increasing wages and to declines in the
29:1057:90436:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:enrollment rates of adolescents.  While we cannot assess if the risk effect could have later mitigated
29:1058:90538:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the  negative  wage  effect  on  human  capital  accumulation  that  was  evident  during  the  program’s
29:1059:90643:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:phase-in, our results do support the idea that policies that support households in smoothing incomes
29:1060:90743:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:without raising wages, will also increase school investments.  Our results also speak to the design
29:1061:90842:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of  such  programs:  welfare  effects  can  be  maximized  by  making  access  to  work  transparent  and
29:1062:90947:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:reliable, and by differentially targeting such programs at villages that are more regularly affected
29:1063:91047:17:0:72:160:544:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:by adverse shocks.

46:1518:113850:0:35:88:176:709:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:APPENDIX
46:1519:113858:35:25:72:209:674:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:A    Data Appendix
46:1520:113876:25:20:72:162:649:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A.1    YLS data
46:1521:113891:20:14:72:540:629:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The Young Lives survey was collected between 2002 and 2013-14 in Andhra Pradesh, a state in the
46:1522:113986:14:13:72:540:615:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:south of India.  Three rounds of data were available at the time of writing this article, and given our
46:1523:114089:13:14:72:540:602:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:focus on school age children we restrict our analysis to rounds 2 (2007) and 3 (2009-10).  Summary
46:1524:114187:14:13:72:506:588:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:statistics for the variables used in this analysis are reported in Table C.1 of this Appendix.
46:1525:114281:13:14:88:539:575:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The data contains various features that are crucial to estimating a production function (and
46:1526:114373:14:13:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:specifically the complementarity parameters) of cognitive skills.  First of all YLS performs different
46:1527:114475:13:14:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cognitive tests: a Peabody Picture Vocabulary Test (PPVT), a math test, a reading comprehension
46:1528:114570:14:14:72:540:534:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:test (EGRA), a Cognitive Development Assessment (CDA) and a verbal test (CLOZE). The test
46:1529:114659:14:13:72:540:520:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:scores of all these tests are internally standardized.  Over time and across cohorts, different tests
46:1530:114760:13:14:72:540:507:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:are being administered.  For the younger cohort we use the PPVT and CDA as measurements of
46:1531:114850:14:13:72:540:493:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:past cognition, and the PPVT, the math test and the EGRA for current cognition.  For the older
46:1532:114944:13:14:72:540:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cohort, we use the PPVT and the math test as measurements for past cognition, and the PPVT,
46:1533:115035:14:13:72:540:466:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the math test and the CLOZE for current cognition.  We use reported time in school and studying
46:1534:115130:13:14:72:540:453:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:as the only investment variable in our production function.  Finally, we use the years of education
46:1535:115229:14:0:72:521:439:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:completed by the mother and the father of each child as measurements for parental cognition.
